<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Cape Cod</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<th scope="row">Area</th>

</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Cape Cod</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Cape_(geography)" title="Cape (geography)">geographic cape</a> extending into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> from the southeastern corner of mainland <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, in the northeastern United States. Its historic, maritime character and ample beaches attract heavy tourism during the summer months.</p>
<p>As defined by the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Commission" title="Cape Cod Commission">Cape Cod Commission</a>'s enabling legislation, Cape Cod is conterminous with <a href="/wiki/Barnstable_County,_Massachusetts" title="Barnstable County, Massachusetts">Barnstable County, Massachusetts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> It extends from <a href="/wiki/Provincetown,_Massachusetts" title="Provincetown, Massachusetts">Provincetown</a> in the northeast to <a href="/wiki/Woods_Hole,_Massachusetts" title="Woods Hole, Massachusetts">Woods Hole</a> in the southwest, and is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth, Massachusetts">Plymouth</a> to the northwest.</p>
<p>Since 1914, Cape Cod has been separated from the mainland by the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Canal" title="Cape Cod Canal">Cape Cod Canal</a>. The canal cuts 17.5 miles (28.2 km) roughly across the base of the peninsula, though small portions of the Cape Cod towns of <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Massachusetts" title="Bourne, Massachusetts">Bourne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Massachusetts" title="Sandwich, Massachusetts">Sandwich</a> lie on the mainland side of the canal. Two highway bridges cross the Cape Cod Canal: the <a href="/wiki/Sagamore_Bridge" title="Sagamore Bridge">Sagamore Bridge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Bridge" title="Bourne Bridge">Bourne Bridge</a>. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Canal_Railroad_Bridge" title="Cape Cod Canal Railroad Bridge">Cape Cod Canal Railroad Bridge</a> carries <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_freight_car" title="Railway freight car">railway freight</a> and limited passenger services onto the Cape. Cape territory is divided into fifteen towns with many villages.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Region_of_Cape_Cod_and_the_Islands">Region of Cape Cod and the Islands <span id="Region_of_Cape_Cod_and_Islands"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Region of Cape Cod and the Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4200" data-file-width="3400" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg/220px-Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg/330px-Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg/440px-Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_-_Landsat_7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Cape and Islands</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like Cape Cod itself, the islands south of the Cape have evolved from whaling and trading areas to become resort destinations, attracting wealthy families, celebrities, and other tourists. These include the large nearby islands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nantucket" title="Nantucket">Nantucket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha's Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a>, which have grown in population by 6.8 percent and 10.3 percent, respectively, between 2000 and 2010 while the year-round population of Barnstable County dropped 3 percent according to the Census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Both islands are also famous summer tourist destinations, commonly accessed by ferry from several locations on the cape. The phrases <b>Cape Cod and the Islands</b> and <b>the Cape and Islands</b> are often used to describe the whole region of Barnstable County, <a href="/wiki/Dukes_County,_Massachusetts" title="Dukes County, Massachusetts">Dukes County</a> (including Martha's Vineyard and the smaller <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Islands" title="Elizabeth Islands">Elizabeth Islands</a>), and Nantucket County.</p>
<p>Several small islands right off Cape Cod, including <a href="/wiki/Monomoy_Island" title="Monomoy Island">Monomoy Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monomoscoy_Island,_Massachusetts" title="Monomoscoy Island, Massachusetts">Monomoscoy Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Popponesset_Island,_Massachusetts" title="Popponesset Island, Massachusetts">Popponesset Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seconsett_Island,_Massachusetts" title="Seconsett Island, Massachusetts">Seconsett Island</a>, are also in Barnstable County.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Forbes_family" title="Forbes family">Forbes family</a>-owned <a href="/wiki/Naushon_Island" title="Naushon Island">Naushon Island</a> was first purchased by <a href="/wiki/John_Murray_Forbes" title="John Murray Forbes">John Murray Forbes</a>. Naushon is one of the Elizabeth Islands, many of which are privately owned. One of the publicly accessible Elizabeths is the southernmost island in the chain, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuttyhunk" title="Cuttyhunk">Cuttyhunk</a>, with a year-round population of 52 people. Several prominent families have established compounds or estates on the larger islands, making these islands some of the wealthiest resorts in the Northeast, yet they retain much of the early merchant trading and whaling culture.</p>
<p>Cape Cod in particular is a popular retirement area; 27.8% of the population of Barnstable County is 65 years old or older.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and the average age of residents is the highest of any area in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By voter registration numbers, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> outnumber <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> by less in the three counties than in the whole of Massachusetts, to varying degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The bulk of the land in the area is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glacial" title="Glacial">glacial</a> <a href="/wiki/Terminal_moraine" title="Terminal moraine">terminal moraine</a> and represents the southernmost extent of glacial coverage in southeast New England; similar glacial formations make up Long Island in New York and <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">Block Island</a> in Rhode Island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_political_divisions">Geography and political divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography and political divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SandyNeckDunes.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/SandyNeckDunes.JPG/275px-SandyNeckDunes.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/SandyNeckDunes.JPG/413px-SandyNeckDunes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/SandyNeckDunes.JPG/550px-SandyNeckDunes.JPG 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SandyNeckDunes.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The dunes on <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Neck_Cultural_Resources_District" title="Sandy Neck Cultural Resources District">Sandy Neck</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">barrier beach</a> that helps prevent <a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">coastal erosion</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography_and_boundaries">Physical geography and boundaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Physical geography and boundaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The name "Cape Cod", as it was first used in 1602, applied only to the very tip of the peninsula. It remained that way for 125 years, until the "Precinct of Cape Cod" was incorporated as the Town of Provincetown. No longer in "official" use over the ensuing decades, the name came to mean all of the land east of the Manomet and Scusset rivers – essentially along the line that became the Cape Cod Canal. The creation of the canal separated the majority of the peninsula from the mainland. Most agencies, including the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Commission" title="Cape Cod Commission">Cape Cod Commission</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA), treat the Cape as an island with regard to disaster preparedness, groundwater management, and the like.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCG_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-USCG-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Cape Codders tend to refer to the land on the mainland side of the canal as "off-Cape", though the legal delineation of Cape Cod, coincident to the boundaries of Barnstable County, includes portions of the towns of Bourne and Sandwich that are located north of the canal.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Bay" title="Cape Cod Bay">Cape Cod Bay</a> lies in between Cape Cod and the mainland – bounded on the north by a horizontal line between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provincetown" title="Provincetown">Provincetown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marshfield,_Massachusetts" title="Marshfield, Massachusetts">Marshfield</a>. North of Cape Cod Bay (and Provincetown) is <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay" title="Massachusetts Bay">Massachusetts Bay</a>, which contains the <a href="/wiki/Stellwagen_Bank_National_Marine_Sanctuary" title="Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary">Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary</a>, located 5 miles (8 km) north of Provincetown. The Atlantic Ocean is to the east of Cape Cod, and to the southwest of the Cape is <a href="/wiki/Buzzards_Bay" title="Buzzards Bay">Buzzards Bay</a>. The Cape Cod Canal, completed in 1916, connects Buzzards Bay to Cape Cod Bay; its creation shortened the trade route between New York and Boston by 62 miles (100 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cape Cod extends 65 miles (105 km) into the Atlantic Ocean, with a breadth of between 1–20 miles (1.6–32.2 km), and covers more than 400 miles (640 km) of shoreline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Its elevation ranges from 306 feet (93 m) at its highest point, at the top of <a href="/wiki/Pine_Hill_(Barnstable_County,_Massachusetts)" title="Pine Hill (Barnstable County, Massachusetts)">Pine Hill</a>, in the Bourne portion of <a href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Cape_Cod" title="Joint Base Cape Cod">Joint Base Cape Cod</a>, down to sea level.</p>
<p>One of the biggest <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">barrier islands</a> in the world, Cape Cod shields much of the Massachusetts coastline from North Atlantic storm waves. This protection erodes the Cape's shoreline at the expense of its cliffs, while protecting towns from Fairhaven to Marshfield.</p>
<p>Cape Cod and the Islands are part of a continuous <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagic region</a> consisting of a thin line of islands stretching west to include Long Island. This region is historically and collectively known by naturalists as the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Lands" title="Outer Lands">Outer Lands</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Towns_and_villages">Towns and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Towns and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deyo-map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1448" data-file-width="1560" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Deyo-map.jpg/275px-Deyo-map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Deyo-map.jpg/413px-Deyo-map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Deyo-map.jpg/550px-Deyo-map.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deyo-map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Barnstable County historical map, 1890</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cape Cod incorporates all of Barnstable County, which comprises 15 towns: <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Massachusetts" title="Bourne, Massachusetts">Bourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Massachusetts" title="Sandwich, Massachusetts">Sandwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falmouth,_Massachusetts" title="Falmouth, Massachusetts">Falmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mashpee,_Massachusetts" title="Mashpee, Massachusetts">Mashpee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnstable,_Massachusetts" title="Barnstable, Massachusetts">Barnstable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth,_Massachusetts" title="Yarmouth, Massachusetts">Yarmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harwich,_Massachusetts" title="Harwich, Massachusetts">Harwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis,_Massachusetts" title="Dennis, Massachusetts">Dennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brewster,_Massachusetts" title="Brewster, Massachusetts">Brewster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham,_Massachusetts" title="Chatham, Massachusetts">Chatham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orleans,_Massachusetts" title="Orleans, Massachusetts">Orleans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastham,_Massachusetts" title="Eastham, Massachusetts">Eastham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wellfleet,_Massachusetts" title="Wellfleet, Massachusetts">Wellfleet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Truro,_Massachusetts" title="Truro, Massachusetts">Truro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Provincetown,_Massachusetts" title="Provincetown, Massachusetts">Provincetown</a>. Each of these towns include a number of villages; see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barnstable_County" title="Barnstable County">Barnstable County</a> for a complete list.</p>
<p>Barnstable, the most populated municipality on Cape Cod, is the only one to have adopted a city form of government, whose legislative body is an elected 13-member <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FormsOfGov_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FormsOfGov-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CityDates_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-CityDates-11">[11]</a></sup> However, like other smaller Massachusetts cities, Barnstable retained its "Town of Barnstable" moniker. All of the other towns elect a 5-member <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Board_of_Selectmen" title="Board of Selectmen">Board of Selectmen</a> as the executive policy-setting board, and utilize <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_Meeting" title="Town Meeting">Town Meetings</a> as their legislative body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FormsOfGov_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FormsOfGov-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cape_Cod_and_the_Islands">Cape Cod and the Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cape Cod and the Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To the south of Cape Cod lie <a href="/wiki/Nantucket_Sound" title="Nantucket Sound">Nantucket Sound</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nantucket" title="Nantucket">Nantucket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha's Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a>, both large islands; and the mostly privately owned <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Islands" title="Elizabeth Islands">Elizabeth Islands</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sections">Sections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station,_Sunset.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station%2C_Sunset.JPG/275px-Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station%2C_Sunset.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station%2C_Sunset.JPG/413px-Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station%2C_Sunset.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station%2C_Sunset.JPG/550px-Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station%2C_Sunset.JPG 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Harbor_Life_Saving_Station,_Sunset.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old Harbor Life Saving Station, in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_National_Seashore" title="Cape Cod National Seashore">Cape Cod National Seashore</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For most of the 18th, 19th, and 20th centuries, Cape Cod was considered to consist of three sections (see map):</p>
<ul>
<li>The <b>Upper Cape</b> is the part of Cape Cod closest to the mainland, comprising the towns of <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Massachusetts" title="Bourne, Massachusetts">Bourne</a>, sandwich, Falmouth, and Mashpee. Falmouth is the home of the famous <a href="/wiki/Woods_Hole_Oceanographic_Institution" title="Woods Hole Oceanographic Institution">Woods Hole Oceanographic Institution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marine_Biological_Laboratory" title="Marine Biological Laboratory">Marine Biological Laboratory</a> as well as several other research organizations, and is also the most-used ferry connection to Martha's Vineyard. Falmouth is composed of several separate villages, including <a href="/wiki/East_Falmouth,_Massachusetts" title="East Falmouth, Massachusetts">East Falmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falmouth_(CDP),_Massachusetts" title="Falmouth (CDP), Massachusetts">Falmouth Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hatchville,_Massachusetts" title="Hatchville, Massachusetts">Hatchville</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Falmouth,_Massachusetts" title="North Falmouth, Massachusetts">North Falmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teaticket,_Massachusetts" title="Teaticket, Massachusetts">Teaticket</a>, Waquoit, <a href="/wiki/West_Falmouth,_Massachusetts" title="West Falmouth, Massachusetts">West Falmouth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Woods_Hole,_Massachusetts" title="Woods Hole, Massachusetts">Woods Hole</a>, as well as several smaller hamlets that are incorporated into their larger neighbors (e.g., Davisville, Hatchville, Falmouth Heights, Quissett, Sippewissett, and others).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Massachusetts" title="Bourne, Massachusetts">Bourne</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Maritime_Academy" title="Massachusetts Maritime Academy">Massachusetts Maritime Academy</a>, in the village of <a href="/wiki/Buzzards_Bay,_Massachusetts" title="Buzzards Bay, Massachusetts">Buzzards Bay</a>, along the canal, <a href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Cape_Cod" title="Joint Base Cape Cod">Joint Base Cape Cod</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aptucxet_Trading_Post" title="Aptucxet Trading Post">Aptucxet Trading Post</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> the annual <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bourne_Scallop_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bourne Scallop Festival (page does not exist)">Bourne Scallop Festival</a> in September, and, until 1884, was part of Sandwich. Sandwich, the oldest town on Cape Cod, founded in 1637, is home to the <a href="/wiki/Dexter_Grist_Mill" title="Dexter Grist Mill">Dexter Grist Mill</a>, the historic <a href="/wiki/Hoxie_House" title="Hoxie House">Hoxie House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Museums_and_Gardens" title="Heritage Museums and Gardens">Heritage Museums and Gardens</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sandwich_Glass_Museum" title="Sandwich Glass Museum">Sandwich Glass Museum</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mashpee,_Massachusetts" title="Mashpee, Massachusetts">Mashpee</a>, is the home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mashpee_Wampanoag" title="Mashpee Wampanoag">Mashpee Wampanoag</a> tribe of Native Americans.</li>
<li>The <b>Mid-Cape</b> area includes the towns of Barnstable, Yarmouth and Dennis. The area features many beautiful beaches, including warm-water beaches along <a href="/wiki/Nantucket_Sound" title="Nantucket Sound">Nantucket Sound</a>, e.g., Kalmus Beach in Hyannis, which gets its name from one of the inventors of <a href="/wiki/Technicolor" title="Technicolor">Technicolor</a>, Herbert Kalmus. This popular windsurfing destination was bequeathed to the town of Barnstable by Dr. Kalmus on condition that it not be developed, possibly one of the first instances of open-space preservation in the US. The Mid-Cape is also the commercial and industrial center of the region. There are seven villages in Barnstable, including <a href="/wiki/Barnstable_(village),_Massachusetts" title="Barnstable (village), Massachusetts">Barnstable Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centerville,_Massachusetts" title="Centerville, Massachusetts">Centerville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotuit,_Massachusetts" title="Cotuit, Massachusetts">Cotuit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyannis,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis, Massachusetts">Hyannis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marstons_Mills,_Massachusetts" title="Marstons Mills, Massachusetts">Marstons Mills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osterville,_Massachusetts" title="Osterville, Massachusetts">Osterville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Barnstable,_Massachusetts" title="West Barnstable, Massachusetts">West Barnstable</a>, as well as several smaller hamlets that are incorporated into their larger neighbors (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Craigville,_Massachusetts" title="Craigville, Massachusetts">Craigville</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cummaquid,_Massachusetts" title="Cummaquid, Massachusetts">Cummaquid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyannis_Port,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis Port, Massachusetts">Hyannis Port</a>, Santuit, Wianno, and others).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The villages of Yarmouth are <a href="/wiki/South_Yarmouth,_Massachusetts" title="South Yarmouth, Massachusetts">South Yarmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Yarmouth,_Massachusetts" title="West Yarmouth, Massachusetts">West Yarmouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth_Port,_Massachusetts" title="Yarmouth Port, Massachusetts">Yarmouth Port</a>. There are five villages in Dennis, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Dennis,_Massachusetts" title="North Dennis, Massachusetts">North Dennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Dennis,_Massachusetts" title="East Dennis, Massachusetts">East Dennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Dennis,_Massachusetts" title="West Dennis, Massachusetts">West Dennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Port,_Massachusetts" title="Dennis Port, Massachusetts">Dennis Port</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Dennis,_Massachusetts" title="South Dennis, Massachusetts">South Dennis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Lower Cape &amp; Outer Cape</b> traditionally includes all of the rest of the Cape, or the towns of <a href="/wiki/Harwich,_Massachusetts" title="Harwich, Massachusetts">Harwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brewster,_Massachusetts" title="Brewster, Massachusetts">Brewster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham,_Massachusetts" title="Chatham, Massachusetts">Chatham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orleans,_Massachusetts" title="Orleans, Massachusetts">Orleans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastham,_Massachusetts" title="Eastham, Massachusetts">Eastham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wellfleet,_Massachusetts" title="Wellfleet, Massachusetts">Wellfleet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Truro,_Massachusetts" title="Truro, Massachusetts">Truro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Provincetown,_Massachusetts" title="Provincetown, Massachusetts">Provincetown</a>. In the present day, the five outermost towns (Provincetown, Truro, Wellfleet, Eastham and Orleans) are more commonly and collectively known as the <b>"Outer Cape"</b>. This area is home to the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_National_Seashore" title="Cape Cod National Seashore">Cape Cod National Seashore</a>, a national park that encompasses much of the Outer Cape, including the entire east-facing coast from Orleans to Provincetown. The Outer Cape is home to some of the most popular beaches in the United States, such as Nauset Light Beach and Coast Guard Beach in Eastham, Race Point Beach in Provincetown, Ballston Beach in Truro, and Skaket Beach in Orleans. The Outer Cape and the beaches in the area have become infamous for their summertime <a href="/wiki/Great_white_shark" title="Great white shark">great white shark</a> sightings along with numerous other shark species. In the summer of 2012, a tourist was attacked and bitten by a great white shark off Ballston Beach in Truro. The Outer Cape is the least populated area of Cape Cod, though Provincetown has a city-like atmosphere during the summer season. Provincetown has become a major gay &amp; lesbian resort destination – the town is regarded as one of the largest <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> resort communities in the United States. Provincetown is also renowned for its historic fishing fleets and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stellwagen_Bank" title="Stellwagen Bank">Stellwagen Bank</a>, a popular fishing ground and <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">whale watching</a> destination, is located a few miles north of Race Point.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id='"Upper"_and_"Lower"'></span><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Upper.22_and_.22Lower.22">"Upper" and "Lower"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title='Edit section: "Upper" and "Lower"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The terms "Upper Cape" and "Lower Cape", and references to traveling "up Cape" or "down Cape" have long been a source of confusion for the uninitiated Cape Cod visitor, who, mistakenly associating "up" with "north", might get turned around by passages such as these from 1920:</p>
<ul>
<li>"The look of things is more ocean-like if one goes down the Cape to Provincetown."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrigham1920206_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrigham1920206-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Almost every street in Chatham is solidly paved, and the old corner town of the Cape is the natural goal of the traveler coming up the Cape from Provincetown..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brigham1920_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brigham1920-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>There are many theories to explain the apparent paradox. One is that the terms derive from early nautical navigation. When one traveled to the east, one went down the longitudinal scale (toward zero at <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">Greenwich</a>, England). Additionally, prevailing fair weather winds (generally out of the southwest) have been used as the basis for directional descriptions by European settlers and their descendants in eastern North America. That is, one would be traveling "down [wind]" to the east with a westerly wind at one's back. To this day, on nearby Martha's Vineyard, "Up Island" is the western section and "Down Island" is to the east.</p>
<p>The arrival of the railroad during the nineteenth century reinforced the "up/down" concept, as train schedules between Boston and Cape Cod always showed Boston at the top – the timetable for trains headed onto the Cape would be read from the top down, and those of returning trains would be read from the bottom up. Provincetown, therefore, despite being the Cape's northernmost town, was the furthest "down" that one could travel. (The Cape's unique shape brought a new paradox along with the automobile and highway system: when driving "down Cape" on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Route_6" title="US Route 6">US Route 6</a> <i>"eastbound"</i>, the final 30 miles from Orleans to Provincetown takes one in nearly every direction <i>except</i> east.)</p>
<p>The best known colloquial explanation, however, is that the shape of the peninsula as it appears on maps and charts resembles that of a human arm. In that analogy, the southern portion of the Cape represents the <i>"upper arm"</i>, Chatham the elbow, and the north-south portion is the <i>"lower arm"</i>, or forearm. Going further, some say Provincetown is the curled hand, or fist, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_Point" title="Race Point">Race Point</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wood_End_Light" title="Wood End Light">Wood End</a> at its knuckles, and <a href="/wiki/Long_Point_(Cape_Cod)" title="Long Point (Cape Cod)">Long Point</a> at the fingertips.</p>
<p>In the late twentieth century, as the Cape began drawing more vacationers and artists on retreat, the nautical nomenclature and potential confusion over directions have gradually been giving way to the simpler "Outer Cape", although the older terms are still used by some local residents.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:250px; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 100%; background-color: #FFFFF0;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: center;">
<div><i><b>"East of America, there stands in the open Atlantic the last fragment of an ancient and vanished land. Worn by the breakers and the rains, and disintegrated by the wind, it still stands bold."</b></i></div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: center;"><small><a href="/wiki/Henry_Beston" title="Henry Beston">Henry Beston</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Outermost_House" title="The Outermost House">The Outermost House</a></i></small></cite></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2145" data-file-width="2418" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg/220px-Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg/330px-Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg/440px-Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_Landsat_7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cape Cod was formed by retreating glaciers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="687" data-file-width="1200" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg/220px-Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg/330px-Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg/440px-Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geologic_Map_of_Cape_Cod.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geologic makeup of Cape Cod</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The bulk of the land on Cape Cod consists of <a href="/wiki/Glacial_landform" title="Glacial landform">glacial landforms</a>, formed by <a href="/wiki/Terminal_moraine" title="Terminal moraine">terminal moraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outwash_plain" title="Outwash plain">outwash plains</a>. This represents the southernmost extent of glacial coverage in southeast New England; similar glacial formations make up <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">Block Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>. Together, these formations are known as the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Lands" title="Outer Lands">Outer Lands</a>, or more obscurely as the "Isles of Stirling". Geologically speaking, Cape Cod is quite young, having been laid down some 16,000 to 20,000 years ago.</p>
<p>Most of Cape Cod's geological history involves the advance and retreat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurentide_ice_sheet" title="Laurentide ice sheet">Laurentide ice sheet</a> in the late <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> geological era and the subsequent changes in sea level. Using <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">radiocarbon dating</a> techniques, researchers have determined that around 23,000 years ago, the ice sheet reached its maximum southward advance over North America, and then started to retreat. Many <a href="/wiki/Kettle_(landform)" title="Kettle (landform)">kettle ponds</a> – clear, cold lakes – were formed and remain on Cape Cod as a result of the receding glacier. By about 18,000 years ago, the ice sheet had retreated past Cape Cod. By roughly 15,000 years ago, it had retreated past southern New England. When so much of Earth's water was locked up in massive ice sheets, the sea level was lower. Truro's bayside beaches used to be a petrified forest, before it became a beach.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deposition_erosion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="989" data-file-width="900" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Deposition_erosion.jpg/220px-Deposition_erosion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Deposition_erosion.jpg/330px-Deposition_erosion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Deposition_erosion.jpg/440px-Deposition_erosion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deposition_erosion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">Coastal erosion</a> by wave action (colored buff in this map) brings growth elsewhere by <a href="/wiki/Deposition_(geology)" title="Deposition (geology)">deposition</a> of transported sediment (shown in blue).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the ice began to melt, the sea began to rise. Initially, sea level rose quickly, about 15 metres (49 ft) per 1,000 years, but then the rate declined. On Cape Cod, sea level rose roughly 3 metres (9.8 ft) per millennium between 6,000 and 2,000 years ago. After that, it continued to rise at about 1 metre (3.3 ft) per millennium. By 6,000 years ago, the sea level was high enough to start eroding the glacial deposits that the vanished continental ice sheet had left on Cape Cod. The water transported the eroded deposits north and south along the outer Cape's shoreline through a process known as <a href="/wiki/Longshore_drift" title="Longshore drift">longshore drift</a>. Those reworked sediments that moved north went to the tip of Cape Cod. The entire town of Provincetown, at the extreme tip of the Cape, is a <a href="/wiki/Spit_(landform)" title="Spit (landform)">spit</a> consisting largely of deposited marine sediment that was eroded and transported from farther south along the shore. Those sediments that instead moved south created the islands and shoals of Monomoy. So while other parts of the Cape have dwindled from the action of the waves, these parts of the Cape have grown through the <a href="/wiki/Deposition_(geology)" title="Deposition (geology)">deposition</a> of sediment in just the last 6,000 years.</p>
<p>This process continues today. Due to their exposure to the open ocean, the Cape and islands are subject to considerable <a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">coastal erosion</a>. Geologists say that due to erosion, the Cape will be completely submerged by the sea within several thousand years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This erosion causes the washout of beaches and the destruction of the barrier islands; for example, the ocean broke through the barrier island at Chatham during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bob" title="Hurricane Bob">Hurricane Bob</a> in 1991, allowing waves and storm surges to hit the coast with no obstruction. Consequently, the sediment and sand from the beaches is being washed away and deposited elsewhere. While this destroys land in some places, it creates land elsewhere, most noticeably in marshes where sediment is deposited by flowing water.</p>
<p>Cape Cod's aquifer consists of six hydrologically independent <a href="/wiki/Lens_(hydrology)" title="Lens (hydrology)">lenses</a> from which all the towns on the Cape obtain drinking water (except Falmouth, which got 43.5% of its 2015 water from Long Pond).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Contamination with industrial chemicals and pharmaceutical drugs from septic systems is a concern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG/220px-Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG/330px-Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG/440px-Cape_Cod_ISS.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although Cape Cod's weather<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> is typically more moderate than inland locations, on occasion it takes the brunt of extreme weather systems such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blizzard_of_2005" title="Blizzard of 2005">Blizzard of 2005</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bob" title="Hurricane Bob">Hurricane Bob</a>. Because of the influence of the Atlantic Ocean, temperatures are typically a few degrees lower in the summer and a few degrees higher in the winter than the adjacent mainland. A common misconception is that the climate is influenced largely by the warm <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> current; however, that current turns eastward off the coast of Virginia, and the waters off the Cape are more influenced by the cold Canadian <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Current" title="Labrador Current">Labrador Current</a>. As a result, the ocean temperature rarely gets above 65 °F (18 °C), except along the shallow west coast of the Upper Cape and along the southern coast (<a href="/wiki/Nantucket_Sound" title="Nantucket Sound">Nantucket Sound</a>), where water temperatures can sometimes reach 70 °F (21 °C) or higher.</p>
<p>Cape Cod's climate is also known for a delayed spring season, being surrounded by an ocean which is still cold from the winter; however, it is also known for an exceptionally mild fall season (<a href="/wiki/Indian_summer" title="Indian summer">Indian summer</a>), thanks to the ocean remaining warm from the summer. The highest temperature ever recorded on Cape Cod was 104 °F (40 °C) in Provincetown,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and the lowest temperature ever was −12 °F (−24 °C) in Barnstable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The water surrounding Cape Cod moderates winter temperatures nearly enough to extend the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> climate zone to what could be its northernmost limit in eastern North America, as the majority of Cape Cod is in USDA <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">hardiness zone</a> 7a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Consequently, many subtropical indicator plant species typically found in more southerly latitudes are grown there, including <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camellias" title="Camellias">Camellias</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ilex_opaca" title="Ilex opaca">Ilex opaca</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Magnolia_grandiflora" title="Magnolia grandiflora">Magnolia grandiflora</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Albizia_julibrissin" title="Albizia julibrissin">Albizia julibrissin</a></i>. However, Cape Cod falls below the 72 °F (22 °C) threshold, as the warmest month, July, averages around 68.25 °F (20.14 °C). Therefore, the climate may be better characterized as either a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_climate" title="Maritime climate">maritime climate</a> or a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_continental" title="Humid continental">humid continental</a> climate (particularly on the northern coast of the upper and mid cape, which is somewhat sheltered from the cooler onshore wind to the south).</p>
<p>Precipitation on Cape Cod and the islands of Martha's Vineyard and Nantucket is the lowest in the New England region, averaging slightly less than 40 inches (100 cm) a year (most parts of New England average 42 to 46 inches (110 to 120 cm)). This is due to storm systems which move across western areas, building up in mountainous regions, and dissipating before reaching the coast where the land has leveled out. The region does not experience a greater number of sunny days, however, as the number of cloudy days is the same as inland locales, in addition to increased fog. On average, roughly 27 inches (69 cm) of snow, which is about 17 inches (43 cm) less than Boston, falls in an average winter.</p>
<p>Once every five or six years, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a>, accompanied by very high and potentially damaging winds and heavy rain, will strike the region. About once every 11 or 12 years a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a> brings damaging winds and <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surges</a> to the region. Several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 3</a> storms have struck Cape Cod since record-keeping began, such as a <a href="/wiki/1869_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Six" title="1869 Atlantic hurricane season">hurricane in 1869</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1938_New_England_hurricane" title="1938 New England hurricane">1938 New England hurricane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carol" title="Hurricane Carol">Hurricane Carol</a> in 1954. Strong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 2</a> storms, such as the <a href="/wiki/1869_Saxby_Gale" title="1869 Saxby Gale">1869 Saxby Gale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Edna" title="Hurricane Edna">Hurricane Edna</a> in 1954, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bob" title="Hurricane Bob">Hurricane Bob</a> in 1991, also caused considerable damage. Notable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 1</a> storms include the <a href="/wiki/1944_Great_Atlantic_hurricane" title="1944 Great Atlantic hurricane">1944 Great Atlantic hurricane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">Hurricane Donna</a> in 1960. Other notable storms include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_September_Gale_of_1815" title="Great September Gale of 1815">Gale of 1815</a>, which would likely have been rated a strong hurricane on the Saffir-Simpson scale, and the so-called "<a href="/wiki/1991_Perfect_Storm" title="1991 Perfect Storm">Perfect Storm</a>" of October 31, 1991. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/February_2013_nor%27easter" title="February 2013 nor'easter">February 2013 nor'easter</a> produced winds in excess of 80 miles per hour (130 km/h) and dropped over 24 inches (61 cm) of snow on some parts of Cape Cod. The storm knocked out power to tens of thousands of Cape Cod residents, some for up to two weeks.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_population">Native population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Native population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cape Cod has been the home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wampanoag_people" title="Wampanoag people">Wampanoag</a> Native American people for many centuries. They survived off the sea and were accomplished farmers. They understood the principles of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_forest_management" title="Sustainable forest management">sustainable forest management</a>, and were known to light <a href="/wiki/Controlled_burn" title="Controlled burn">controlled fires</a> to keep the underbrush in check. They helped the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrims_(Plymouth_Colony)" title="Pilgrims (Plymouth Colony)">Pilgrims</a>, who arrived in the fall of 1620, survive at their new <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a>.</p>
<p>The Wampanoag lost their lands through continued <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wampanoag_people" title="Wampanoag people">purchase and expropriation by the English colonists</a>. The documentary <i>Natives of the Narrowland</i> (1993), narrated by actress <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julie_Harris_(American_actress)" title="Julie Harris (American actress)">Julie Harris</a>, shows the history of the Wampanoag people through Cape Cod archaeological sites.</p>
<p>In 1974, the Mashpee Wampanoag Tribal Council was formed to articulate the concerns of those with Native American ancestry. They petitioned the federal government in 1975 and again in 1990 for official recognition of the Mashpee Wampanoag as a tribe. In May 2007, the Wampanoag tribe was federally recognized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_by_Europeans">Discovery by Europeans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Discovery by Europeans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cape Cod was a landmark for early explorers. It may have been the "Promontory of <a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a>" mentioned by the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> voyagers (985–1025). The Manomet River area (taken up by the western end of the Cape Cod Canal in the early 20th century) is claimed by some to have been visited by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leif_Eiriksson" title="Leif Eiriksson">Leif Eiriksson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and a stone wall<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wikimapia_link_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wikimapia_link-31">[31]</a></sup> discovered in Provincetown in 1805 is also claimed to have been built by his younger brother <a href="/wiki/Thorvald_Eiriksson" title="Thorvald Eiriksson">Thorvald Eiriksson</a> around 1007 AD,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norse_Wall_Cape_Links_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norse_Wall_Cape_Links-32">[32]</a></sup> when the keel of his ship was repaired in the harbor, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_saga" title="Norse saga">Norse sagas</a>. He was killed later in the same journey, and is said to have been returned to this spot for burial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> However, there is no tangible support of the presence of Norse voyagers in Cape Cod,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and the view is not generally accepted by archaeologists or historians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a> approached it from the south in 1524. He named <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha's Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a> Claudia, after <a href="/wiki/Claude_of_France" title="Claude of France">Claude of France</a>, the wife of <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I of France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-History-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1525, Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_Gomes" title="Estêvão Gomes">Estêvão Gomes</a> called it Cabo de la Arenas while sailing under the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish crown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weber1992_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weber1992-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1602, <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Gosnold" title="Bartholomew Gosnold">Bartholomew Gosnold</a> named the tip Cape Cod, the surviving term and the ninth oldest English place-name in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">Samuel de Champlain</a> charted its sand-silted harbors in 1606, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> landed there in 1609. Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith</a> noted it on his map of 1614, and at last the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrims_(Plymouth_Colony)" title="Pilgrims (Plymouth Colony)">Pilgrims</a> entered the "Cape Harbor" and – contrary to the popular myth of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Rock" title="Plymouth Rock">Plymouth Rock</a> – made their first landing near present-day <a href="/wiki/Provincetown,_Massachusetts" title="Provincetown, Massachusetts">Provincetown</a> on November 11, 1620. Nearby, in what is now <a href="/wiki/Eastham,_Massachusetts" title="Eastham, Massachusetts">Eastham</a>, they had their first encounter with Native Americans.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cape Cod was among the first places settled by the English in North America. The Cape's fifteen towns developed slowly, aside from <a href="/wiki/Barnstable,_Massachusetts" title="Barnstable, Massachusetts">Barnstable</a> (1639), <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Massachusetts" title="Sandwich, Massachusetts">Sandwich</a> (1637), and <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth,_Massachusetts" title="Yarmouth, Massachusetts">Yarmouth</a> (1639). The final town to be established on the Cape was <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Massachusetts" title="Bourne, Massachusetts">Bourne</a> in 1884, breaking off from Sandwich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Provincetown was a group of huts until the 18th century. A channel from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay" title="Massachusetts Bay">Massachusetts Bay</a> to <a href="/wiki/Buzzards_Bay" title="Buzzards Bay">Buzzards Bay</a> is shown on Southack's map of 1717. The present Cape Cod Canal was slowly developed from 1870 to 1914. The federal government purchased it in 1928.</p>
<p>The Cape's vegetation was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depauperate" title="Depauperate">depauperate</a> and trees were scarce by the time that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_Thoreau" title="Henry Thoreau">Henry Thoreau</a> saw Cape Cod during his four visits over 1849 to 1857,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> because of early colonial settlement and intensive land use. The settlers heated by fires, and it took 10 to 20 cords (40 to 80 m³) of wood to heat a home, so they cleared most of Cape Cod of timber early on. They planted familiar crops, but these were unsuited to Cape Cod's thin, glacially derived soils. For instance, much of Eastham was planted to wheat. The settlers practiced burning of woodlands to release nutrients into the soil. Improper and intensive farming led to erosion and the loss of topsoil. Farmers grazed their cattle on the grassy dunes of coastal Massachusetts, only to watch "in horror as the denuded sands 'walked' over richer lands, burying cultivated fields and fences." Dunes on the outer Cape became more common, and many harbors filled in with eroded soils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1800, much of Cape Cod's firewood had to be transported by boat from <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>. The paucity of vegetation was worsened by the raising of <a href="/wiki/Merino" title="Merino">merino</a> sheep that reached its peak in New England around 1840. The early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> occurred through much of Massachusetts and <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, but it mostly bypassed Cape Cod due to a lack of significant water power in the area. The Cape developed as a large fishing and <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> center as a result, and also because of its geographic position. After 1860 and the opening of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_West" title="American West">American West</a>, farmers abandoned agriculture on the Cape. By 1950, forests had recovered to an extent not seen since the 18th century.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="1001" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg/300px-Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg/450px-Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg/600px-Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cranberry_Picking_on_Cape_Cod.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cranberry" title="Cranberry">Cranberry</a> picking in 1906</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cape Cod became a summer haven for city dwellers beginning at the end of the 19th century. Improved rail transportation made the towns of the Upper Cape accessible to <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Bostonians</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Massachusetts" title="Bourne, Massachusetts">Bourne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falmouth,_Massachusetts" title="Falmouth, Massachusetts">Falmouth</a>. At the beginning of the twentieth century, the Northeastern mercantile elite built many large, shingled "cottages" along <a href="/wiki/Buzzards_Bay" title="Buzzards Bay">Buzzards Bay</a>. The relaxed summer environment offered by Cape Cod was highlighted by writers including <a href="/wiki/Joseph_C._Lincoln" title="Joseph C. Lincoln">Joseph C. Lincoln</a>, who published novels and countless short stories about Cape Cod folks in popular magazines such as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturday_Evening_Post" title="Saturday Evening Post">Saturday Evening Post</a></i> and the <i>Delineator</i>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">Guglielmo Marconi</a> made the first transatlantic <a href="/wiki/Wireless" title="Wireless">wireless</a> transmission originating in the United States from Cape Cod, at <a href="/wiki/Wellfleet,_Massachusetts" title="Wellfleet, Massachusetts">Wellfleet</a>. The beach below the bluffs where his station was located is now called <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Beach" title="Marconi Beach">Marconi Beach</a>. In 1914, he began construction of a new transatlantic wireless receiver station in <a href="/wiki/Chatham,_Massachusetts" title="Chatham, Massachusetts">Chatham</a> and a companion transmitter station in <a href="/wiki/Marion,_Massachusetts" title="Marion, Massachusetts">Marion</a>. In 1920, the stations were acquired by RCA and, in 1921, Chatham began operations as a maritime radio station communicating to ships at sea using the callsign <a href="/wiki/WCC_(radio_station)" title="WCC (radio station)">WCC</a>. WCC supported the communications of <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Earhart" title="Amelia Earhart">Amelia Earhart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Byrd" title="Richard E. Byrd">Admiral Byrd</a>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/LZ_129_Hindenburg" title="LZ 129 Hindenburg">Hindenburg</a></i>. Marconi chose Chatham due to its vantage point on the Atlantic Ocean, surrounded on three sides by water. <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cronkite" title="Walter Cronkite">Walter Cronkite</a> narrated a 17-minute documentary in 2005 about the history of the Chatham Station.</p>
<p>Much of the east-facing Atlantic seacoast of Cape Cod consists of wide, sandy beaches. In 1961, a significant portion of this coastline, already slated for housing subdivisions, was made a part of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_National_Seashore" title="Cape Cod National Seashore">Cape Cod National Seashore</a> by President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>. It was protected from private development and preserved for public use. Large portions are open to the public, including the Marconi Site in <a href="/wiki/Wellfleet,_Massachusetts" title="Wellfleet, Massachusetts">Wellfleet</a>. This is a park encompassing the site of the first two-way transoceanic radio transmission from the United States. (<a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> used Marconi's equipment for this transmission.)</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Compound" title="Kennedy Compound">Kennedy Compound</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hyannis_Port,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis Port, Massachusetts">Hyannis Port</a> was President Kennedy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summer_White_House" title="Summer White House">summer White House</a> during his presidency, and the Kennedy family continues to maintain residences on the compound. President <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a> maintained a summer home in the Gray Gables section of Bourne. Other notable residents of Cape Cod have included actress <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julie_Harris_(American_actress)" title="Julie Harris (American actress)">Julie Harris</a>, US Supreme Court justice <a href="/wiki/Louis_Brandeis" title="Louis Brandeis">Louis Brandeis</a>, figure skater <a href="/wiki/Todd_Eldredge" title="Todd Eldredge">Todd Eldredge</a>, composer and radio personality <a href="/wiki/Canary_Burton" title="Canary Burton">Canary Burton</a>, and novelists <a href="/wiki/Norman_Mailer" title="Norman Mailer">Norman Mailer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">Kurt Vonnegut</a>. Influential natives included patriot <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Otis,_Sr." title="James Otis, Sr.">James Otis</a>, historian and writer <a href="/wiki/Mercy_Otis_Warren" title="Mercy Otis Warren">Mercy Otis Warren</a>, jurist <a href="/wiki/Lemuel_Shaw" title="Lemuel Shaw">Lemuel Shaw</a>, and naval officer <a href="/wiki/John_Percival" title="John Percival">John Percival</a>.</p>
<p>On October 28, 2015, a 6-foot-long blue shark was found stranded on a Provincetown beach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lighthouses_of_Cape_Cod">Lighthouses of Cape Cod</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Lighthouses of Cape Cod">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</div>

</div>
<div style="position:absolute;top:76.917%;left:14.119%">
