</div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USA_Mass_Cape_Cod_location_map.svg" title="File:USA Mass Cape Cod location map.svg"></a></div>
The lighthouses of Cape Cod</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:320px; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 100%; background-color: #FFFFF0;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: center;">
<div><i><b>"Lighthouses, from ancient times, have fascinated members of the human race. There is something about a lighted beacon that suggests hope and trust and appeals to the better instincts of mankind."</b></i></div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: center;"><small><a href="/wiki/Edward_Rowe_Snow" title="Edward Rowe Snow">Edward Rowe Snow</a></small></cite></div>
<p>Cape Cod's coastline has been called an "ocean graveyard" from Chatham to Provincetown, a mere fifty-mile stretch of sea containing over 3,000 shipwrecks, due to its dangerously hidden and constantly moving shoals located just off-shore. Indeed, there have been more than 1,000 wrecks between Truro and Wellfleet alone, including that of the <i><a href="/wiki/Whydah_Gally" title="Whydah Gally">Whydah Gally</a></i>. The famed pirate ship of <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Bellamy" title="Samuel Bellamy">"Black Sam" Bellamy</a> was laden with over 4.5 <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a> (4.1 <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">metric tons</a>) of treasure when she went down in 1717, killing him and all but two of his 145 fellow sailors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beginning in 1797, <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouses</a> were erected along Cape Cod to aid in navigation. <a href="/wiki/Highland_Light" title="Highland Light">Highland Light</a> (or Cape Cod Light) is the oldest and tallest of these, and remains as one of a number of working lighthouses on Cape Cod and the Islands. Many of Cape Cod's earliest lighthouses featured a light tower that was attached directly to – and centered on the roof of – the <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse_keeper" title="Lighthouse keeper">keeper's dwelling</a>. A stairway to the lantern room was accessible only from the top floor of the house. This came to be known as a <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_style" title="Cape Cod style">Cape Cod style</a> lighthouse, yet today, the only fully intact specimens are on the west coast of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lighthousefriends_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-lighthousefriends-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nauset_Light,_Eastham,_MA,_Cape_Cod.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="2051" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nauset_Light%2C_Eastham%2C_MA%2C_Cape_Cod.jpg/275px-Nauset_Light%2C_Eastham%2C_MA%2C_Cape_Cod.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nauset_Light%2C_Eastham%2C_MA%2C_Cape_Cod.jpg/413px-Nauset_Light%2C_Eastham%2C_MA%2C_Cape_Cod.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nauset_Light%2C_Eastham%2C_MA%2C_Cape_Cod.jpg/550px-Nauset_Light%2C_Eastham%2C_MA%2C_Cape_Cod.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nauset_Light,_Eastham,_MA,_Cape_Cod.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nauset Light, erected here in 1923 and moved to a safer location in 1996, is on the National Register of Historic Places</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of Cape Cod's lighthouses are operated by the U.S. Coast Guard, with some exceptions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Nauset_Light" title="Nauset Light">Nauset Light</a>, which has been owned since 1997 by the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_National_Seashore" title="Cape Cod National Seashore">Cape Cod National Seashore</a> (National Park Service) and operated since 2004 in partnership between that agency and the non-profit Nauset Light Preservation Society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1996, both Highland Light and Nauset Light were moved further from the shore because they were each at risk of being lost due to erosion by the sea. Highland Light, then 110 ft (34 m) from the ocean, was moved 450 ft (140 m) to the west, and Nauset Light, 37 ft (11 m) from the bluff, was moved 300 ft (91 m) west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The lighthouses of Cape Cod include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Upper Cape: <a href="/wiki/Nobska_Light" title="Nobska Light">Nobska Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wing%27s_Neck_Light" title="Wing's Neck Light">Wing's Neck Light</a> (privately owned), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland_Ledge_Light" title="Cleveland Ledge Light">Cleveland Ledge Light</a> (also private).</li>
<li>Mid Cape: <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Neck_Light" title="Sandy Neck Light">Sandy Neck Light</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyannis_Harbor_Light" title="Hyannis Harbor Light">Hyannis Harbor Light</a>, Lewis Bay Light (or Hyannis Inner Harbor Light, also private), <a href="/wiki/Bishop_and_Clerks_Light" title="Bishop and Clerks Light">Bishop and Clerks Light</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lighthouse_Inn_(West_Dennis,_Massachusetts)" title="Lighthouse Inn (West Dennis, Massachusetts)">West Dennis Light</a> (formerly the Bass River Light)</li>
<li>Lower Cape: <a href="/wiki/Long_Point_Light" title="Long Point Light">Long Point Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wood_End_Light" title="Wood End Light">Wood End Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Race_Point_Light" title="Race Point Light">Race Point Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highland_Light" title="Highland Light">Highland Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauset_Light" title="Nauset Light">Nauset Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Three_Sisters_of_Nauset" title="Three Sisters of Nauset">Three Sisters of Nauset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayo_Beach_Light" title="Mayo Beach Light">Mayo Beach Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billingsgate_Island_Light" title="Billingsgate Island Light">Billingsgate Island Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Light" title="Chatham Light">Chatham Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monomoy_Point_Light" title="Monomoy Point Light">Monomoy Point Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stage_Harbor_Light" title="Stage Harbor Light">Stage Harbor Light</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1201" data-file-width="1500" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg/275px-Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg/413px-Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg/550px-Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Cod_Bourne_Bridge_and_Railroad_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Bridge" title="Bourne Bridge">Bourne Bridge</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Canal" title="Cape Cod Canal">Cape Cod Canal</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Canal_Railroad_Bridge" title="Cape Cod Canal Railroad Bridge">Cape Cod Canal Railroad Bridge</a> in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cape Cod is connected to the mainland by a pair of canal-spanning highway bridges, the <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Bridge" title="Bourne Bridge">Bourne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sagamore_Bridge" title="Sagamore Bridge">Sagamore</a> that were constructed in the 1930s (replacing a 1912 drawbridge). The two parallel road bridges are four miles apart, with the Bourne Bridge to the west, and the Sagamore to the east. The bridges form a bottleneck, resulting in traffic backups of several miles during the tourist season - especially going on-cape at the beginning of the weekend and off-cape at the end of the weekend.</p>
<p>The entire Cape is roughly bisected lengthwise by <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_6" title="U.S. Route 6">U.S. Route 6</a>, locally known as the Mid-Cape Highway and officially as the Grand Army of the Republic Highway.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_and_water">Air and water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Air and water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Commercial air service to Cape Cod operates out of <a href="/wiki/Barnstable_Municipal_Airport" title="Barnstable Municipal Airport">Barnstable Municipal Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Provincetown_Municipal_Airport" title="Provincetown Municipal Airport">Provincetown Municipal Airport</a>. General aviation airports are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chatham_Municipal_Airport" title="Chatham Municipal Airport">Chatham Municipal Airport</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Falmouth_Airpark" title="Falmouth Airpark">Falmouth Airpark</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Airfield" title="Cape Cod Airfield">Cape Cod Airfield</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marstons_Mills" title="Marstons Mills">Marstons Mills</a>, Barnstable</li>
</ul>
<p>There is one military airport at <a href="/wiki/Otis_Air_National_Guard_Base" title="Otis Air National Guard Base">Otis Air National Guard Base</a>.</p>
<p>There are <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> connections from Boston to Provincetown, as well as from Hyannis and Woods Hole to the islands.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Cape Cod Regional Transit Authority">Cape Cod Regional Transit Authority</a> operates a year-round public bus system comprising three long distance routes and a local bus in Hyannis and Barnstable Village. From mid June until October, additional local routes are added in Falmouth and Provincetown. CCRTA also operates Barnstable County's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act" title="Americans with Disabilities Act">ADA</a>-required <a href="/wiki/Paratransit" title="Paratransit">paratransit</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dial-a-ride" title="Dial-a-ride">dial-a-ride</a>) service, under the name "B-Bus."</p>
<p>Long distance bus service is available through <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth_and_Brockton_Street_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plymouth and Brockton Street Railway (page does not exist)">Plymouth and Brockton Street Railway</a>, with regular service to downtown Boston and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logan_Airport" title="Logan Airport">Logan Airport</a>, as well as less frequent service to Provincetown. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan_Bus_Lines" title="Peter Pan Bus Lines">Peter Pan Bus Lines</a> also runs long distance service to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T.F._Green_Airport" title="T.F. Green Airport">T.F. Green Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence, Rhode Island</a>; New York City; and service between Logan Airport, Boston <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">South Station</a>, and Woods Hole.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_service">Rail service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rail service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The third bridge over the Cape Cod Canal is a <a href="/wiki/Vertical-lift_bridge" title="Vertical-lift bridge">vertical-lift</a> railroad bridge, providing an alternative land transport option.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/CapeFlyer" title="CapeFlyer">CapeFlyer</a> is a seasonal passenger rail service between Boston and Hyannis that operates on summer weekends from <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day" title="Memorial Day">Memorial Day</a> through <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a>.</p>
<p>Daily passenger rail service to Cape Cod ended in June 1959. In 1978, the tracks east of South Dennis were abandoned and replaced with the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Rail_Trail" title="Cape Cod Rail Trail">Cape Cod Rail Trail</a>. Another bike path, the <a href="/wiki/Shining_Sea_Bikeway" title="Shining Sea Bikeway">Shining Sea Bikeway</a>, was built over abandoned tracks between Woods Hole and Falmouth in 1975, and in 2008 the 7.4-mile long (11.9 km) rail line between Falmouth and North Falmouth was removed and the right-of-way converted into an extension of the Shining Sea Bikeway.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Central_Railroad" title="Cape Cod Central Railroad">Cape Cod Central Railroad</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heritage_railroad" title="Heritage railroad">heritage railroad</a> on Cape Cod. The service is primarily tourist-oriented and includes a dinner train over a scenic route between Hyannis and the Cape Cod Canal lasting about 2½ hours round trip. Limited service is also provided to Buzzards Bay and from there to North Falmouth.</p>
<p>Active freight service remains in the Upper Cape area in Sandwich and in Bourne, largely due to a trash transfer station located at <a href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Cape_Cod" title="Joint Base Cape Cod">Joint Base Cape Cod</a> along the Bourne-Falmouth rail line. In 1986, <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> operated a seasonal service in the summer from New York City to Hyannis called the <i><a href="/wiki/Cape_Codder_(train)" title="Cape Codder (train)">Cape Codder</a></i>. From 1988, Amtrak and the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Department_of_Transportation" title="Massachusetts Department of Transportation">Massachusetts Department of Transportation</a> increased service to a daily frequency,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> until service ended in 1996, leaving a gap until the current CapeFlyer service began in 2013.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle">Bicycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bicycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bicycle and pedestrian access to the Cape is possible via a sidewalk on the southbound side of the <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Bridge" title="Bourne Bridge">Bourne Bridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> There are a number of dedicated bike trails and paths around the Cape, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Rail_Trail" title="Cape Cod Rail Trail">Cape Cod Rail Trail</a> - South Dennis to Wellfleet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Colony_Rail_Trail" title="Old Colony Rail Trail">Old Colony Rail Trail</a> - Harwich and Chatham, connecting with the Cape Cod Rail Trail</li>
<li>Various trails in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_National_Seashore" title="Cape Cod National Seashore">Cape Cod National Seashore</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>Various trails in <a href="/wiki/Nickerson_State_Park" title="Nickerson State Park">Nickerson State Park</a>, connecting with the Cape Cod Rail Trail</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shining_Sea_Bikeway" title="Shining Sea Bikeway">Shining Sea Bikeway</a> - Woods Hole to North Falmouth</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Canal" title="Cape Cod Canal">Cape Cod Canal</a> path on both sides of the canal</li>
<li>Various unpaved Mid-Cape trails<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>For long-distance biking, the mostly on-road <a href="/wiki/Claire_Saltonstall_Bikeway" title="Claire Saltonstall Bikeway">Claire Saltonstall Bikeway</a> connects Cape Cod to the <a href="/wiki/Charles_River_Bike_Path" title="Charles River Bike Path">Charles River Bike Path</a> in Boston.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg/275px-Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg/413px-Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg/550px-Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sailboat_in_Hyannis_Harbor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hyannis,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis, Massachusetts">Hyannis Harbor</a> on <a href="/wiki/Nantucket_Sound" title="Nantucket Sound">Nantucket Sound</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cape Cod has a year-round population of about 220,000, and it experiences a tourist season each summer, the beginning and end of which can be roughly approximated as <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day" title="Memorial Day">Memorial Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a>, respectively. Many businesses specifically target summer visitors, although the "on season" has been expanding somewhat in recent years due to <a href="/wiki/Indian_summer" title="Indian summer">Indian Summer</a>, reduced lodging rates, the number of people visiting the Cape after Labor Day who have no school-age children, and the elderly—reducing the true "off season" to six or seven months. In the late 20th century, tourists and owners of second homes began visiting the Cape more and more in the spring and fall, softening the definition of the high season and expanding it somewhat.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Provincetown,_Massachusetts" title="Provincetown, Massachusetts">Provincetown</a> at the tip of Cape Cod berths the original East Coast <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">whale watching</a> fleet (Dolphin Fleet) who patrol the <a href="/wiki/Stellwagen_Bank_National_Marine_Sanctuary" title="Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary">Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary</a>. The fleet guarantee a whale sighting (mostly <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sei_whale" title="Sei whale">sei whale</a>, and the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">North Atlantic right whale</a>) and is the only federally certified operation qualified to rescue whales. Provincetown has also long been known as an art colony, attracting writers and artists. The town is home to the Cape's most attended art museum, the <a href="/wiki/Provincetown_Art_Association_and_Museum" title="Provincetown Art Association and Museum">Provincetown Art Association and Museum</a>.</p>
<p>Cape Cod is a popular destination for beachgoers from all over, with 559.6 miles (900.6 km) of coastline. Beaches—both public and private—are easily accessible. The Cape has upwards of sixty public beaches, many of which offer parking for non-residents for a daily fee (in summer). The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_National_Seashore" title="Cape Cod National Seashore">Cape Cod National Seashore</a> has 40 miles (64 km) of sandy beach and many walking paths.</p>
<p>Cape Cod is also popular for its outdoor activities, such as beach walking, biking, boating, fishing, go-karts, golfing, kayaking, miniature golf, and unique shopping. There are 27 public, daily-fee golf courses and 15 private courses on Cape Cod.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bed_and_breakfast" title="Bed and breakfast">Bed and breakfasts</a> or vacation houses are often used for lodging.</p>
<p>Each summer, the <a href="/wiki/Naukabout_Music_Festival" title="Naukabout Music Festival">Naukabout Music Festival</a> is held at the Barnstable County Fair Grounds located in <a href="/wiki/East_Falmouth,_Massachusetts" title="East Falmouth, Massachusetts">East Falmouth</a>, typically during the first weekend of August. The festival features local, regional, and national talent, along with food, arts, and family-friendly activities. Some particularly well-known Cape products and industries include <a href="/wiki/Cranberry" title="Cranberry">cranberries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">shellfish</a> (particularly <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a> and clams), and <a href="/wiki/Lobster_fishing" title="Lobster fishing">lobstering</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport_fishing">Sport fishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sport fishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cape Cod is known around the world as a spring-to-fall destination for sport anglers. Among the species most widely pursued are <a href="/wiki/Striped_bass" title="Striped bass">striped bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bluefish" title="Bluefish">bluefish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_bluefin_tuna" title="Atlantic bluefin tuna">bluefin tuna</a>, false albacore (<a href="/wiki/Little_tunny" title="Little tunny">little tunny</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bonito" title="Bonito">bonito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tautog" title="Tautog">tautog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flounder" title="Flounder">flounder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Summer_flounder" title="Summer flounder">fluke</a>. The Cape Cod Bay side of the Cape, from Sandwich to Provincetown, has numerous harbors, saltwater creeks, and shoals that hold bait fish and attract the larger game fish, such as striped bass, bluefish and bluefin tuna.</p>
<p>The outer edge of the Cape, from Provincetown to Falmouth, faces the open Atlantic from Provincetown to Chatham, and then the more protected water of Nantucket and Vineyard Sounds, from Chatham to Falmouth. The bays, harbors and shoals along this coastline also provide a robust habitat for game species, and during the late summer months warm-water species such as <a href="/wiki/Mahi-mahi" title="Mahi-mahi">mahi-mahi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a> will also appear on the southern edge of Cape Cod's waters. Nearly every harbor on Cape Cod hosts sport fishing charter boats, which run from May through October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-test-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the most popular fishing spots on the East Coast is the Cape Cod Canal. Striped bass, especially, in season attract anglers from far and wide. A large part of the attraction involves ease of access. Ample free parking exists all along the waterway, and the banks are a short walk from one's vehicle. This reduces fishing to the basics – a pole and a few lures.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Cape has nine amateur baseball franchises playing within Barnstable County in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Baseball_League" title="Cape Cod Baseball League">Cape Cod Baseball League</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Wareham_Gatemen" title="Wareham Gatemen">Wareham Gatemen</a> also play in the Cape Cod Baseball League in nearby <a href="/wiki/Wareham,_Massachusetts" title="Wareham, Massachusetts">Wareham</a> in <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_County,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth County, Massachusetts">Plymouth County</a>. The league's beginning is unsettled, even fanciful. Without any basis whatsoever, some claim a start date of 1875. However, the first Cape Cod League formed in Sandwich in 1910. It did not last. Three years later - in 1913 - another Cape Cod Baseball League organized. This venture lasted two years. In 1916, a third attempt at league play barely got off the ground. Then, in 1923, an initial four teams met in Hyannis and started a successful federation along the lines of the present league. Outstanding players from throughout the region competed until the war effort led to a shutdown in 1940. In 1946, the local town teams from the prewar County Twilight League and Lower Cape Cod League organized under the Cape Cod Baseball League banner. As the years passed, local players were moved aside by outside college stars. Finally, in 1963, the league became a wholly summer collegiate circuit sanctioned by the National Collegiate Athletic Association with some Major Leagues financial support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The current teams in the league are the <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Braves" title="Bourne Braves">Bourne Braves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brewster_Whitecaps" title="Brewster Whitecaps">Brewster Whitecaps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Anglers" title="Chatham Anglers">Chatham Anglers</a> (formerly the Chatham Athletics), <a href="/wiki/Cotuit_Kettleers" title="Cotuit Kettleers">Cotuit Kettleers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falmouth_Commodores" title="Falmouth Commodores">Falmouth Commodores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harwich_Mariners" title="Harwich Mariners">Harwich Mariners</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyannis_Harbor_Hawks" title="Hyannis Harbor Hawks">Hyannis Harbor Hawks</a> (formerly the Hyannis Mets), <a href="/wiki/Orleans_Firebirds" title="Orleans Firebirds">Orleans Firebirds</a> (formerly the Orleans Cardinals), <a href="/wiki/Wareham_Gatemen" title="Wareham Gatemen">Wareham Gatemen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth%E2%80%93Dennis_Red_Sox" title="Yarmouth–Dennis Red Sox">Yarmouth–Dennis Red Sox</a>. <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">MLB scouts</a> frequent the games in the summer, looking for stars of the future.</p>
<p>Along with the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Baseball_League" title="Cape Cod Baseball League">Cape Cod Baseball League</a> and the new Junior Hockey League team, the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Islanders" title="Cape Cod Islanders">Cape Cod Islanders</a>, many high school players are being recruited as well. Barnstable and Harwich have each sent multiple players to Division 1 colleges for baseball. Harwich has also won three state titles since 1996 (1996, 2006, 2007). Bourne and Sandwich, rivals in hockey, have each won state championships recently, Bourne in 2004 and Sandwich in 2007. Nauset, Barnstable, and Martha's Vineyard are also state hockey powerhouses. Barnstable and Falmouth hold the title of having <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_high_school_football_rivalries_(100_years%2B)" title="List of high school football rivalries (100 years+)">one of the longest Thanksgiving football rivalries in the country</a>. The teams have played each other every year on Thanksgiving since 1895. High school football teams on the Cape have also recently become successful and the region has also become a hot-spot for college recruiting. In 2011, four high school football teams from the Cape won state championships in their respective divisions; Dennis-Yarmouth (Division 2A), Bourne (Division 3A), Mashpee (Division 4), as well as Nantucket and Upper Cape Cod Tech (Division 5). Also, numerous other Cape schools have made appearances in the football state championship game recently, including Barnstable in 2012, Martha's Vineyard in 2008, Cape Cod Tech in 2006, and Dennis-Yarmouth in 2013. The Bourne and Barnstable girls' volleyball teams are two of the best teams in the state and Barnstable is considered one of the best programs in the country. Bourne won the state title in 2003 and 2007, and Barnstable has won 12 Division 1 state titles in the past 13 years and has won the state title the three years in a row (2011–2013). In the 2010 cross country season, Sturgis Charter Public School's Division 4 cross country team remained virtually unbeaten throughout their running season.</p>
<p>The Cape is home to the Cape Cod Frenzy, a team in the <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(2000%E2%80%93present)" title="American Basketball Association (2000–present)">American Basketball Association</a>.</p>
<p>Soccer on Cape Cod is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Crusaders" title="Cape Cod Crusaders">Cape Cod Crusaders</a>, playing in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USL_Premier_Development_League" title="USL Premier Development League">USL Premier Development League</a> (PDL) based in Hyannis. In addition, a summer Cape Cod Adult Soccer League (CCASL) is active in several towns on the Cape.</p>
<p>Cape Cod is the home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Cubs" title="Cape Cod Cubs">Cape Cod Cubs</a>, a new junior league hockey team that is based out of <a href="/wiki/Hyannis,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis, Massachusetts">Hyannis</a> at the new community center being built on Bearses Way.</p>
<p>The end of each summer is marked with the running of the <a href="/wiki/Falmouth_Road_Race" title="Falmouth Road Race">Falmouth Road Race</a>, held on the third Saturday in August. It draws about 10,000 runners to the Cape and showcases the finest runners in the world (mainly for the large purse that the race is able to offer). The race is 7.2 miles (11.6 km) long, which is a non-standard distance. The reason for the unusual distance is that the man who thought the race up (Tommy Leonard) was a bartender who wanted a race along the coast from one bar (The Cap'n Kidd in Woods Hole) to another (The Brothers Four in Falmouth Heights). While the bar in Falmouth Heights is now the British Beer Company, the race still starts at the front door of the Cap'n Kidd in Woods Hole and now finishes at the beach in Falmouth Heights. Prior to the Falmouth race is an annual 5-mile (8.0 km) race through Brewster called the Brew Run, held early in August.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Most Cape Cod towns have a few elementary schools, one or two middle schools and one large public high school that serves the entire town. Exceptions to this include <a href="/wiki/Dennis-Yarmouth_Regional_High_School" title="Dennis-Yarmouth Regional High School">Dennis-Yarmouth Regional High School</a>, located in Yarmouth, which serves the two towns in its name; <a href="/wiki/Monomoy_Regional_High_School" title="Monomoy Regional High School">Monomoy Regional High School</a>, located in Harwich and serving that town as well as Chatham; and <a href="/wiki/Nauset_Regional_High_School" title="Nauset Regional High School">Nauset Regional High School</a> in Eastham, which serves the towns of Brewster, Orleans, Eastham, Wellfleet, Truro, and Provincetown. <a href="/wiki/Bourne_High_School" title="Bourne High School">Bourne High School</a> serves students in that town, which includes the villages of Sagamore, Sagamore Beach, and Buzzards Bay. <a href="/wiki/Barnstable_High_School" title="Barnstable High School">Barnstable High School</a> is the Cape's largest. <a href="/wiki/Sturgis_Charter_Public_School" title="Sturgis Charter Public School">Sturgis Charter Public School</a>, a public school in Hyannis that was featured in <i>Newsweek</i> magazine's "Best High Schools" ranking, offers the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate_Diploma_Programme" title="International Baccalaureate Diploma Programme">International Baccalaureate Diploma Programme</a> in their junior and senior year and is open to students from as far away as <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth, Massachusetts">Plymouth</a>. The Cape also has two vocational high schools. One is the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Regional_Technical_High_School" title="Cape Cod Regional Technical High School">Cape Cod Regional Technical High School</a> in Harwich, and the other is <a href="/wiki/Upper_Cape_Cod_Regional_Technical_High_School" title="Upper Cape Cod Regional Technical High School">Upper Cape Cod Regional Technical High School</a> in Bourne.</p>
<p>In 1976 the Cape schools and districts petitioned the Massachusetts Legislature to create an educational collaborative, the Cape Cod Collaborative, to facilitate cooperation and efficiency in providing gifted and talented, and special needs programs. With locations in Osterville and Bourne the Cape Cod Collaborative provides transportation services, professional development, autism support, developmental training, itinerant services and an alternative education program. Each summer, in cooperation with the Massachusetts Maritime Academy, it operates a science-based program for gifted and talented students from around the Cape.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mashpee_High_School" title="Mashpee High School">Mashpee High School</a> is home to the Mashpee Chapter of SMPTE, the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Motion_Picture_and_Television_Engineers" title="Society of Motion Picture and Television Engineers">Society of Motion Picture and Television Engineers</a>. This chapter is the first and only high school chapter in the world to be a part of this organization and has received much recognition within the Los Angeles broadcasting industry as a result.</p>
<p>In addition to public schools, Cape Cod has a wide range of private schools. The town of Barnstable has Trinity Christian Academy, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Academy" title="Cape Cod Academy">Cape Cod Academy</a>, St. Francis Xavier Preparatory School, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II_High_School_(Massachusetts)" title="Pope John Paul II High School (Massachusetts)">Saint John Paul II High School</a>. Bourne offers the Waldorf School of Cape Cod, Orleans offers the Lighthouse Charter School for elementary and middle school students, and Falmouth offers <a href="/wiki/Falmouth_Academy" title="Falmouth Academy">Falmouth Academy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Riverview_School" title="Riverview School">Riverview School</a> is located in East Sandwich and is a special co-ed boarding school which serves students as old as 22 who have learning disabilities. Another specialized school is the <a href="/wiki/Penikese_Island" title="Penikese Island">Penikese Island</a> School, located in the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Islands" title="Elizabeth Islands">Elizabeth Islands</a> off southwestern Cape Cod, which serves struggling and troubled teenage boys.</p>
<p>Cape Cod contains three institutions of higher education. One is the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Community_College" title="Cape Cod Community College">Cape Cod Community College</a> located in West Barnstable. The second is <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Maritime_Academy" title="Massachusetts Maritime Academy">Massachusetts Maritime Academy</a> in the village of <a href="/wiki/Buzzards_Bay,_Massachusetts" title="Buzzards Bay, Massachusetts">Buzzards Bay</a>. Massachusetts Maritime Academy is the oldest continuously operating maritime college in the United States. The third is <a href="/wiki/Bridgewater_State_University" title="Bridgewater State University">Bridgewater State University</a>, which opened a satellite campus in <a href="/wiki/South_Yarmouth,_Massachusetts" title="South Yarmouth, Massachusetts">South Yarmouth</a> in January 2015. The school will provide 40 undergraduate and graduate courses leading to the completion of bachelor's degree and master's degree programs in Early Childhood Education, Educational Leadership, Secondary Education, Reading, and Special Education. The campus will also offer Certificate Programs in Business and Social Work. Beginning in the Summer 2015, the campus will begin to offer undergraduate credit courses in History.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture_and_art">In popular culture and art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: In popular culture and art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Codder_(cocktail)" title="Cape Codder (cocktail)">Cape Codder cocktail</a> is named after the peninsula; both are notable for <a href="/wiki/Cranberry" title="Cranberry">cranberry</a>. Cape Cod also generated a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_(house)" title="Cape Cod (house)">Cape style house</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_style" title="Cape Cod style">Cape lighthouse</a>.</p>
<p>The virtues of Cape Cod are extolled in the song "<a href="/wiki/Old_Cape_Cod" title="Old Cape Cod">Old Cape Cod</a>".</p>
<p>Artist <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hopper" title="Edward Hopper">Edward Hopper</a> owned a summer house in Truro, and painted numerous Cape scenes including <i>Corn Hill</i> (1930), <i>Highland Light, North Truro</i> (1930), <i>Rich's House</i> (1930), <i>High Road</i> (1931), <i>House on Dune Edge</i> (1931), <i>Cold Storage Plant</i> (1933), and <i>Cottages at North Truro</i> (1936).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Norman_Mailer" title="Norman Mailer">Norman Mailer</a>'s 1984 noir thriller and murder mystery novel <i><a href="/wiki/Tough_Guys_Don%27t_Dance_(novel)" title="Tough Guys Don't Dance (novel)">Tough Guys Don't Dance</a></i> is set in Provincetown on Cape Cod.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Cole_Porter" title="Cole Porter">Cole Porter</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Do_It,_Let%27s_Fall_in_Love" title="Let's Do It, Let's Fall in Love">Let's Do It</a>," "cold Cape Cod clams 'gainst their wish do it."</p>
<p>In 1996, the Commonwealth of Massachusetts allowed the creation of a "Cape &amp; Islands" registration plate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<p><a class="external text" href="http://pubs.usgs.gov/gip/capecod/" rel="nofollow">Geologic History of Cape Cod, Massachusetts</a>, by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> (USGS)</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Cod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Cumbler, John T. <i>Cape Cod: An Environmental History of a Fragile Ecosystem.</i> Amherst, MA: University of Massachusetts Press, 2014.</li>
<li>Freeman, Frederick. (1860). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=D9uEQbPZB9YC" rel="nofollow"><i>The History of Cape Cod: The Annals of Barnstable County and of Its Several Towns (Vol. 1)</i></a>. Harvard University.</li>
<li>Freeman, Frederick. (1862). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=vIzF-SN29ksC" rel="nofollow"><i>The History of Cape Cod: The Annals of Barnstable County and of Its Several Towns (Vol. 2)</i></a>. Harvard University.</li>
<li>LeBlanc, D.R. (1986). <i>Ground-water resources of Cape Cod, Massachusetts</i> [Hydrologic Investigations Atlas HA-692]. Reston, Va.: U.S. Department of the Interior, U.S. Geological Survey.</li>
<li>Massey, A.J., C.S. Carlson, and D.R. LeBlanc. (2006). <i>Ground-water levels near the top of the water-table mound, western Cape Cod, Massachusetts, 2002–04</i> [Scientific Investigations Report 2006-5054]. Reston, VA: U.S. Department of the Interior, U.S. Geological Survey.</li>
<li>Masterson, J.P. and J.W. Portnoy. (2005). <i>Potential changes in ground-water flow and their effects on the ecology and water resources of the Cape Cod National Seashore, Massachusetts</i> [General Information Product 13]. Reston, VA: U.S. Department of the Interior, U.S. Geological Survey.</li>
<li>Walter, D.A. and A.T. Whealan. (2005). <i>Simulated water sources and effects of pumping on surface and ground water, Sagamore and Monomoy flow lenses, Cape Cod, Massachusetts</i> [Scientific Investigations Report 2004-5181]. Reston, VA: U.S. Department of the Interior, U.S. Geological Survey.</li>
